$$f(A) = -0.7726 A^2 - 0.7726 A + 0.7402 \cos(\log(A+1))$$

Key features of the GT:
1. It has an $A^2$ term (polynomial)
2. It has an $A$ term (polynomial)
3. It has $\cos(\log(A+1))$ — a very specific transcendental function
4. It does NOT depend on $t$

The $\cos(\log(A+1))$ term is crucial. This is a very specific basis function that cannot be replicated by:
- $\sin(cA + d)$ — different functional form
- $\exp(cA)$ — different functional form
- $\log(cA+1)$ — different functional form
- Rational functions of $A$ — different functional form

Let me scan through candidates looking for any that contain $\cos(\log(\cdot))$:

Going through all 55 candidates, I see the following basis functions used:
- Polynomials/rational functions in $A$
- $\sin(A \cdot c + c)$ — sinusoidal in $A$ (NOT $\cos(\log(A+1))$)
- $\exp(A \cdot c)$ — exponential in $A$
- $\log(A \cdot c + 1)$ — logarithmic in $A$
- $A^c$ — power law
- Various $t$-dependent terms (which can be zeroed out)

**None of the candidates contain $\cos(\log(\cdot))$.**

The critical question: can any combination of the available basis functions exactly equal $\cos(\log(A+1))$?

- $\sin(cA + d)$: This is periodic in $A$ with constant period. $\cos(\log(A+1))$ is NOT periodic in $A$ (the "period" stretches as $A$ grows). These are fundamentally different functions. No match.
- $\exp(cA)$: Monotonic (or zero), cannot match an oscillatory function.
- $\log(cA+1)$: Monotonic, cannot match oscillatory behavior.
- $A^c$: Power functions are monotonic for $A > 0$, cannot match oscillations.
- Rational functions: Also cannot produce the oscillatory behavior of $\cos(\log(A+1))$.

No finite combination of $\sin(cA)$, $\exp(cA)$, $\log(cA+1)$, $A^c$, and rational functions can exactly equal $\cos(\log(A+1))$ for all $A \geq 0$. These are linearly independent basis function families.

For candidates with $t$-dependent terms: we can set those coefficients to zero, but the remaining $A$-dependent parts still lack $\cos(\log(A+1))$.

Let me double-check Candidate 1 more carefully as it has the most terms with $\sin$:
$$\frac{A^2 c_0 + A c_3 + c_4\sin(Ac_5+c_6) + c_7}{Ac_1+c_2}$$

This is a rational function plus $\sin$ terms divided by a linear denominator. Even with optimal constants, $\sin(cA+d)/(eA+f)$ cannot equal $\cos(\log(A+1))$ — they have fundamentally different functional forms.

Similarly for all other candidates — none contain the $\cos(\log(\cdot))$ basis function needed.
